2:27:1385:28:28:273:338:616:12:Times:12:Times:ABSTRACT
2:28:1393:28:14:72:540:588:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:The valuation of government debt is subject to strategic uncertainty, stemming from investors' sentiments.
2:29:1499:14:14:72:540:574:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Pessimistic lenders, fearing default, bid down the price of debt. This leaves a government with a higher
2:30:1603:14:14:72:540:560:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:debt burden, increasing the likelihood of default and thus confirming the pessimism of lenders. This
2:31:1703:14:14:72:540:546:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:paper studies the interaction of monetary policy and debt fragility. It asks: do monetary interventions
2:32:1806:14:14:72:540:532:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:mitigate debt fragility? The answer depends in part on the nature of monetary policy, particularly the
2:33:1908:14:14:72:540:518:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:ability of the monetary authority to commit to future state contingent actions. With commitment to
2:34:2006:14:14:72:540:504:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:a state contingent policy, the monetary authority can indeed overcome strategic uncertainty. Under
2:35:2104:14:42:72:460:490:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:discretion, debt fragility remains unless reputation effects are sufficiently strong.
2:36:2189:42:14:72:153:448:12:g_d0_f1:12:g_d0_f1:Antoine Camous

3:53:2537:20:15:110:514:577:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:The valuation of government debt is subject to strategic uncertainty, stemming from investors’ sen-
3:54:2636:15:16:96:514:562:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:timents.  Pessimistic lenders, fearing default, bid down the price of debt.  This leaves a government with
3:55:2742:16:15:96:514:546:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:a higher debt burden, increasing the likelihood of default and thus confirming the pessimism of lenders.
3:56:2846:15:15:96:514:531:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:This paper studies the interaction of monetary policy and debt fragility.  It asks:  do monetary interven-
3:57:2952:15:16:96:514:516:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:tions mitigate debt fragility?  The answer depends in part on the nature of monetary policy, particularly
3:58:3057:16:15:96:514:500:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:the ability of the monetary authority to commit to future state contingent actions.  With commitment
3:59:3157:15:15:96:514:485:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:to a state contingent policy, the monetary authority can indeed overcome strategic uncertainty.  Under
3:60:3259:15:23:96:420:470:9:g_d0_f7:9:g_d0_f7:discretion, debt fragility remains unless reputation effects are sufficiently strong.
3:61:3344:23:17:86:540:447:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f10:Keywords:monetary policy, seignorage, inflation, sovereign debt, self-fulfilling debt crisis, sunspot equi-
3:62:3451:17:33:71:97:430:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:libria.

3:64:3498:57:27:71:184:340:14:g_d0_f11:14:g_d0_f11:1    Introduction
3:65:3515:27:16:96:514:313:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:But there is another message I want to tell you.  Within our mandates,  the ECB is ready to do
3:66:3609:16:17:96:515:297:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f9:whatever it takes to preserve the euro.  And believe me,  it will be enough.[Mario Draghi, July
3:67:3704:17:27:96:123:280:10:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f12:2012]1
3:68:3710:27:17:86:539:253:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This paper studies the interaction of fiscal and monetary policy in the presence of strategic uncertainty
3:69:3815:17:16:71:539:236:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:over the value of government debt.  In real economies, beliefs of investors about the likelihood of government
3:70:3925:16:15:71:539:220:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:default,  and  hence  the  value  of  its  debt,  can  be  self-fulfilling.   Pessimistic  investors,  fearing  government
3:71:4047:15:16:82:540:205:6:g_d0_f13:8:g_d0_f14:∗Thanks  to  Costas  Azariadis,  Marco  Bassetto,  Piero  Gottardi,  Immo  Schott,  Ramon  Marimon  and  seminar  participants
3:72:4173:16:13:72:540:189:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:at  the  Pennsylvania  State  University,  European  University  Institute,  Rimini  Center  For  Economic  Analysis  (RCEF  2014),
3:73:4304:13:13:72:540:176:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:XIX Workshop On Macroeconomics Dynamics, Congress of the European Economic Association 2014, the Fall 2014 CU/PSU
3:74:4417:13:9:72:431:163:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:Macroeconomics Conference, the EUI Alumni Conference 2014 and the University of Mannheim.
3:75:4506:9:11:83:389:154:6:g_d0_f13:8:g_d0_f14:†Department of Economics, European University Institute, antoine.camous@eui.eu
3:76:4584:11:10:83:388:143:6:g_d0_f13:8:g_d0_f14:‡Department of Economics, Pennsylvania State University, russellcoop@gmail.com
3:77:4662:10:12:83:540:133:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:1This statement is an excerpt from the address of Mario Draghi, President of the European Central Bank, at a financial
3:78:4780:12:0:72:163:121:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:conference, in July 2012.
4:79:4806:0:17:72:540:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:default, will only purchase government debt if there is a sufficient risk premium.  The resulting increase in
4:80:4915:17:17:72:540:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the cost of funds makes default more likely.2Pessimism can be self-fulfilling even if fundamentals are sound
4:81:5023:17:17:71:324:725:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:enough that an equilibrium without default exists as well.
4:82:5081:17:16:86:539:708:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:These results hold for real economies, in which the intervention of a monetary authority is not considered.
4:83:5188:16:17:71:539:692:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Does this debt fragility exist in a nominal economy?  The presence of a monetary authority can provide an
4:84:5293:17:17:71:539:675:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:alternative source of revenue through an inflation tax and perhaps use its influence to stabilize real interest
4:85:5404:17:17:71:539:658:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:rates.  Can the monetary authority act to eliminate strategic uncertainty over the value of sovereign debt?  If
4:86:5515:17:16:71:539:641:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:so, will it have an incentive to do so?  The answers to these questions are relevant for assessing the relevance
4:87:5627:16:17:71:539:625:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of these results on strategic uncertainty in debt markets and for guidance on the conduct of monetary policy.
4:88:5736:17:17:86:539:608:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The overlapping generations model with active fiscal and monetary interventions provides a framework
4:89:5836:17:17:71:539:591:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:for analysis.  The model is structured to highlight strategic uncertainty in the pricing of government debt
4:90:5943:17:16:71:539:574:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:stemming from the default choice of a government.  By construction, there is an equilibrium without default,
4:91:6051:16:17:71:377:558:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:and in general there are other equilibria with state contingent default.
4:92:6123:17:17:86:539:541:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The monetary authority intervenes through transfers to the fiscal entity,  financed by an inflation tax.
4:93:6227:17:16:71:539:524:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The  monetary  intervention  has  a  number  of  influences.   First,  the  inflation  tax  delivers  real  resources  to
4:94:6348:16:17:71:539:508:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the government, thus reducing the debt burden from taxation.  Second, the realized value of inflation alters
4:95:6456:17:17:71:539:491:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the real value of debt and consequently the debt burden left to the fiscal authority.  Third, it may impact
4:96:6563:17:17:71:370:474:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:expectations of future inflation and thus the tax base for seignorage.
4:97:6633:17:16:86:539:457:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Given these transfers and its outstanding obligations, the fiscal authority chooses to default or not.  Our
4:98:6740:16:17:71:539:441:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:analysis emphasizes the dependence of this default decision, and thus the extent of strategic uncertainty, on
4:99:6849:17:17:71:539:424:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the conduct of monetary policy.  As our results develop, the capacity of the monetary authority to stabilize
4:100:6957:17:17:71:539:407:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:sovereign  debt  markets  relies  on  the  interplay  of  the  inflation  and  expectation  channels,  not  on  on  the
4:101:7076:17:16:71:260:390:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:collection of revenue from the inflation tax.
4:102:7121:16:17:86:539:374:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:We undertake the analysis under alternative monetary policy regimes.  If there is complete discretion in
4:103:7225:17:17:71:539:357:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:monetary policy or if the monetary authority commits to a strict inflation target, the strategic uncertainty
4:104:7333:17:17:71:318:340:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:in the real economy is present in the monetary economy.
4:105:7388:17:16:86:539:323:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:However, if the monetary authority can commit to a particular state contingent transfer function, given
4:106:7491:16:17:71:539:307:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:an inflation target, then its intervention can stabilize debt valuations.  Specifically, this policy is designed to
4:107:7606:17:17:71:539:290:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:eliminate all equilibria with state contingent default, preserving the one in which debt is risk-free.  Interest-
4:108:7719:17:17:71:539:273:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:ingly, this desired intervention does not “bail-out” the fiscal authority.  Rather, the countercyclical nature
4:109:7829:17:16:71:539:256:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of this policy induces an accommodative fiscal stance in times of low productivity.  This intervention leans
4:110:7937:16:17:71:442:240:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:against negative sentiments of investors and preserves the fundamental price of debt.
4:111:8022:17:17:86:539:223:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This policy is reminiscent of the commitment of the European Central Bank, reflected in the above quote
4:112:8125:17:16:71:540:206:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of Mario Draghi, to undertakewhatever it takesto counter pessimistic self-fulfilling expectations on Eurozone
4:113:8234:16:17:71:539:190:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:sovereign debt markets.  Under the intervention we design, the central bank uses its commitment power to
4:114:8338:17:17:71:539:173:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:have a stabilizing influence on sovereign’s debt valuations.  In equilibrium, no actual intervention is required
4:115:8450:17:15:71:539:156:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:and debt is uniquely valued.  Moreover, this policy does not endanger the primary objective of the central
4:116:8556:15:12:83:540:141:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:2This interaction between beliefs and default is central to Calvo (1988);  and other contributions that followed,  including
4:117:8680:12:0:72:322:129:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:Cole and Kehoe (2000), Roch and Uhlig (2012) and Cooper (2012).
5:118:8744:0:17:72:357:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:bank, to anchor inflation expectations around an inflation target.
5:119:8810:17:17:86:539:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:We  present  conditions  such  that  this  policy  is  credible,  so  that  commitment  to  its  implementation  is
5:120:8925:17:17:72:540:725:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:not needed.  The implementation requires a punishment:  we consider the case where a deviating monetary
5:121:9028:17:16:72:540:708:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:authority returns to a strict inflation target regime.  Not surprisingly, all else the same, a patient monetary
5:122:9139:16:17:72:540:692:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:authority is less likely to deviate.  But there is another element in the analysis:  the higher the risk of self-
5:123:9252:17:17:72:539:675:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:fulfilling debt crisis in the inflation target regime, themorecredible is the promise of the central bank to
5:124:9360:17:17:72:357:658:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:interveneex postto counter pessimistic beliefs on debt valuation.
5:125:9425:17:16:86:539:641:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Other  analysis  examine  possible  strategies  for  central  banks  to  address  self-fulling  debt  crises.   Calvo
5:126:9542:16:17:71:539:625:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:(1988) extends his real economy to include a discussion of inflation as a form of partial default.  He imposes
5:127:9652:17:17:71:539:608:10:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f12:an exogenous motive of money demand and an explicit cost of inflation function that affects net output.3
5:128:9756:17:17:71:539:591:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Calvo (1988) argues that there may exist multiple equilibria in the determination of inflation and the nominal
5:129:9866:17:16:71:539:574:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:interest rate on government debt.  For this analysis, there is no interaction between fiscal and monetary debt
5:130:9976:16:17:71:124:558:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:repudiation.
5:131:9988:17:17:86:539:541:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Corsetti and Dedola (2013) augments Calvo’s framework to study the interaction of fiscal and monetary
5:132:10089:17:16:71:539:524:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:policy.   Their  analysis  retains  some  of  the  central  features  of  Calvo’s  model,  including  exogenous  money
5:133:10207:16:17:71:540:508:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:demand and costlyex postinflation.  They argue that monetary interventions through the printing press will
5:134:10313:17:17:71:539:491:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:not generally resolve debt fragility.  But, the central bank, through its holding of government debt, can have
5:135:10423:17:17:71:168:474:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:a stabilizing influence.
5:136:10447:17:16:86:539:457:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Aguiar, Amador, Farhi, and Gopinath (2013) build a nominal economy with a debt roll-over crisis, as in
5:137:10549:16:17:71:539:441:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Cole and Kehoe (2000).  They investigate the optimal degree of conservativeness of the central bank (as in
5:138:10655:17:17:71:539:424:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Rogoff (1985)) as a tool to address inefficient debt crisis.  Moderate inflation aversion contains the occurrence
5:139:10768:17:17:71:395:407:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of self-fulfilling debt crisis and restrains the inflation bias in normal times.
5:140:10848:17:16:86:539:390:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Our analysis differs from these others papers in a couple of fundamental ways:  (i) endogenous money
5:141:10948:16:17:71:539:374:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:demand and (ii) no assumedex  postcosts of inflation.  In particular, money demand in our model comes
5:142:11049:17:17:71:540:357:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:from  intertemporal  savings  of  households  and  the  cost  of  inflation  occurs  through  theex  anteeffect  of
5:143:11164:17:17:71:539:340:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:anticipated  inflation  on  labor  supply.   The  endogeneity  of  money  demand  is  central  to  our  results.   Our
5:144:11282:17:16:71:539:323:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:environment displays a complementarity between expected and realized inflation.  Money demand reflects
5:145:11384:16:17:71:540:307:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f10:expected inflation.  The absence of an explicitex postcost of inflation provides a strong incentive forex post
5:146:11494:17:17:71:539:290:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:inflation.  With these two features, under discretion, the central bank can be cornered into a high inflation
5:147:11603:17:17:71:539:273:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:equilibrium, unable to either inflate nominal debt or provide additional resources via seignorage, along with
5:148:11712:17:16:71:539:256:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:a low inflation equilibrium.4Accordingly, our analysis of fragility in debt markets builds upon the critical
5:149:11820:16:17:71:235:240:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:need to anchor inflation expectations.
5:150:11858:17:17:86:539:223:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The paper is structured as follows.  Section 2 describes the economic environment and the fiscal problem
5:151:11962:17:16:71:539:206:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of  the  government.   Section  3  displays  debt  fragility  in  a  benchmark  real  economy.   Section 4  defines  the
5:152:12082:16:17:71:539:190:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:relevant equilibrium concept in the nominal economy and investigates the presence of debt fragility under two
5:153:12191:17:17:71:539:173:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:monetary policy frameworks:  delegation and discretion.  Section 5 characterizes a monetary policy rule that
5:154:12299:17:15:71:539:156:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:can eliminate debt fragility and presents conditions such that this strategy is credible.  Section 6 concludes.
5:155:12410:15:9:83:296:141:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:3Specifically, see equations (16) and (19) in Calvo (1988).
5:156:12469:9:0:83:454:132:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:4This feature of our model is similar to that explored in Chari, Christiano, and Eichenbaum (1998).
6:157:12569:0:27:72:261:759:14:g_d0_f11:14:g_d0_f11:2    Economic Environment
6:158:12594:27:17:72:540:732:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Consider  an  overlapping  generation  economy  with  domestic  and  foreign  agents.   Agents  live  two  periods.
6:159:12709:17:17:72:197:715:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Time is discrete and infinite.
6:160:12739:17:16:86:539:698:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:There are a couple of key components of the model.  First, agents differ in productivity in young age and
6:161:12844:16:17:72:540:682:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:form a demand for savings.  Relatively poor agents hold money as a store of value rather than incurring a
6:162:12949:17:17:72:540:665:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:cost to save through an intermediary.  Importantly, money demand is endogenous, thus making the tax base
6:163:13053:17:16:72:365:648:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:for seignorage dependent on inflation expectations of young agents.
6:164:13120:16:17:86:539:632:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Second the government issues debt each period and faces a choice on how to finance the repayment of its
6:165:13223:17:17:72:508:615:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:obligations.  In particular, the government can tax labor income, print money or default on its debt.
6:166:13324:17:17:86:539:598:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The environment is structured to highlight debt fragility:  there are multiple self-fulfilling values of gov-
6:167:13433:17:33:72:503:581:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:ernment debt.  In this section, we describe the choices of private agents and the fiscal environment.
6:168:13534:33:23:72:190:548:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:2.1    Private Agents
6:169:13555:23:17:72:540:525:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Every period, a continuum of mass 1 of domestic agents (households) is born and lives two periods.  These
6:170:13660:17:17:72:540:508:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:agents  consume  only  when  old  and  their  preferences  are  linear  in  consumption  and  labor  disutility  is
6:171:13775:17:17:72:540:491:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:quadratic.   This  restriction  is  introduced  to  neatly  capture  the  reaction  of  agents  to  government  policy
6:172:13893:17:16:72:105:474:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:choices.
6:173:13901:16:17:86:539:458:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Domestic agents produce a perishable good in both young and old age.  Production is linear.  In youth,
6:174:14003:17:17:72:539:441:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:productivity is heterogenous.  A massνmof agents have low productivityzm= 1.  A massνI= 1−νmof
6:175:14097:17:16:72:539:424:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:agents have high productivityzI=z >1.  In old age, productivityAis stochastic, i.i.d., and common to all
6:176:14201:16:17:72:122:408:10:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f12:old agents.5
6:177:14213:17:17:86:539:391:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Agents have access to two technologies to store value:  money or financially intermediated claims.  Access
6:178:14319:17:17:72:540:374:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:to the latter is costly: agents pay a participation cost Γ for access to intermediaries.  Limited financial market
6:179:14433:17:16:72:540:357:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:participation sorts agents in two groups.  For convenience, we will refer topooragents, who will hold only
6:180:14539:16:17:72:539:341:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f9:moneyin equilibrium, andrichagents, who holdintermediated claimsin equilibrium.  Intermediated claims
6:181:14640:17:17:72:540:324:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:are invested either in nominal government bonds or in a risk-free asset,  e.g.  storage,  that delivers a real
6:182:14750:17:31:72:113:307:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:returnR.

8:263:19662:24:16:72:540:207:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The government is composed of a treasury and a central bank.  Every period, it has to finance a constant

9:286:21139:17:17:72:539:580:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:when these agents are old.10We return to this restriction in our concluding comments.  So the government
9:287:21243:17:30:72:352:563:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:budget constraint under repayment becomes generation specific:
9:288:21305:30:0:204:259:533:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f16:(1 +i) ̃πb=τ
9:289:21317:0:8:261:266:541:10:g_d0_f20:10:g_d0_f20:(
9:290:21318:8:0:266:367:533:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f9:νmAnmo(τ) +νIAnIo(τ)

9:293:21342:7:0:390:396:526:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f16:P
9:294:21343:0:31:405:540:533:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f9:.(12)
9:295:21348:31:17:86:539:502:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Instead of repayment, the government can fully renege on its debt.  But there are two costs of default for
9:296:21454:17:17:71:540:485:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:domestic agents. First, direct costs of default are born by old rich agents, who hold a fractionθof government
9:297:21564:17:16:71:539:468:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:debt.  Second, if the government repudiates its debt, the country suffers from a deadweight loss, as commonly
9:298:21673:16:17:71:540:452:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:assumed in the literature on strategic default.11Formally, aggregate productivity contemporaneously drops
9:299:21778:17:17:71:539:435:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:by a proportional factorγ.  The model excludes punishments involving exclusion from future capital markets.
9:300:21885:17:16:71:539:418:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This is partly to ensure that default effects are contained within a generation but also reflects the quantitative
9:301:21999:16:17:71:389:402:10:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f12:finding that the main force preventing default is the direct output loss.12
9:302:22074:17:17:86:539:385:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:As  the  government  budget  constraint  holds  over  time  for  a  given  generation,  a  decision  to  default  on
9:303:22190:17:17:71:540:368:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:periodtdebt has no direct effect on future generations.  That is, default affects only the welfare of current
9:304:22299:17:16:71:350:351:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:old agents, who otherwise are taxed via seignorage or labor tax.
9:305:22363:16:17:86:539:335:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The government weights the welfare burden of tax distortions against the direct costs and penalty induced
9:306:22468:17:17:71:539:318:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:by the default decision.  Denote byWr(·) the welfare of the economy underrepaymentand byWd(·) under
9:307:22567:17:17:71:419:301:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f9:default.  The decision to default is optimal whenever ∆(·) =Wd(·)−Wr(·)≥0.
9:308:22641:17:16:86:539:284:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Given aggregate productivityA, nominal interest ratei, real money tax basem−1, tax rateτ, money
9:309:22736:16:16:72:540:268:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:printing rateσthat satisfy (12) and the induced inverse inflation rate   ̃π,  the welfare criterionWD(·) for
9:310:22844:16:12:79:540:252:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:10This use of generational budget balance appears in Chari and Kehoe (1990) and Cooper,  Kempf,  and Peled (2010),  for
9:311:22963:12:9:72:540:240:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:example.  An alternative,  as in Cole and Kehoe (2000),  could add more strategic uncertainty through debt rollover.  For an
9:312:23087:9:7:72:531:231:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:analysis of self-fulfilling debt crisis with active debt issuance and maturity management, see Lorenzoni and Werning (2013).
9:313:23211:7:12:79:540:224:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:11Penalties and direct sanctions are central theoretic concepts for enforcement of international asset trade.  See the seminal

9:315:23430:7:12:79:540:205:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:12Empirical evidence regarding reputation costs of default are mixed:  exclusion from international credit markets are short-
9:316:23555:12:10:72:540:193:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:lived and premium following defaults are usually found to be negligible.  An extensive discussion can be found in Trebesch,
9:317:23678:10:9:72:540:183:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:Papaioannou, and Das (2012).  From a theoretical point of view, Bulow and Rogoff (1989) show that reputation mechanisms
9:318:23797:9:0:72:514:174:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:cannot enforce international asset trade, if the government can buy foreign assets as an alternative source of insurance.

10:358:24859:33:24:72:178:429:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:2.3    Assumptions

10:376:25651:17:14:72:540:186:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:is held by foreigners.15The presence of an equilibrium without default provides a convenient benchmark for

10:379:25857:9:13:79:540:153:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:15This assumption is derived using the government budget constraint with no inflation, no fiscal resource from seignorage and
10:380:25982:13:9:72:539:140:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:all debt is held by foreigners (θ= 0).  It implies that there will be an equilibrium without default risk when some of the debt is
10:381:26112:9:9:72:540:131:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:held by domestic agents and when money printing does provide resources to the fiscal authority.  Indeed, domestic holding of

12:439:28614:0:33:361:540:613:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f9:.(22)
12:440:28619:33:16:72:307:580:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Any ̄Asolving this equation is part of an equilibrium.
12:441:28673:16:17:86:539:564:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Denote byG(A) the left side and byZthe right side of  (22).G(·) is continuous on [Al,Ah],G(Al) =
12:442:28769:17:17:71:174:547:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f9:A2l>0 andG(Ah) = 0.
12:443:28788:17:17:86:539:530:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Consistent  with  Assumption  3,  ifZ < A2l=G(Al),  there  is  a  risk  free  interest  rate: ̄A=Aland
12:444:28890:17:16:71:540:513:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:(1 +i) =Ris a solution to (22).  Also, by continuity ofG(·), there is ̄A∈(Al,Ah) such thatG( ̄A) =Z.
12:445:28990:16:17:71:535:497:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Hence there is also an interest rate that carries a risk-premium and that solves the no-arbitrage condition.
12:446:29098:17:17:86:540:480:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Relaxing Assumption 3, ifZ > A2l=G(Al), all equilibria include default risk and thus a risk premium.
12:447:29198:17:17:71:539:463:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Ifbis very high, thenZwill be large as well and there may be no equilibrium in which debt is valued.  If
12:448:29302:17:16:71:539:446:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:debt is valued so that there is a solution to (22), thenG(A)> Zfor someA > Al.  Again, by continuity,
12:449:29403:16:25:71:199:430:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:there is a second equilibrium.
12:450:29433:25:17:86:539:405:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f10:The multiple equilibria of the debt financing problem identified here are welfare ordered. Thefundamental
12:451:29538:17:16:72:540:388:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:equilibrium with certain repayment provides higher utility than any other equilibrium with higher interest
12:452:29644:16:17:72:540:372:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:rate and state contingent default.  In the fundamental equilibrium, repayment is preferred to default in those
12:453:29754:17:17:72:540:355:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:states where default is optimal in the other equilibria.  And in repayment states, lower interest rate in the
12:454:29863:17:16:72:507:338:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:fundamental equilibrium requires lower taxes, hence higher welfare, than under the other equilibria.
12:455:29963:16:17:86:540:322:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Importantly, note that Proposition 1 does not directly restrict the level of debt,b.  As long as debt has
12:456:30068:17:17:72:540:305:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:value, there are multiple equilibria.  The level of debt though cannot be too large.  Else an equilibrium with
12:457:30178:17:17:72:450:288:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:valued debt will not exist, since the government would default for all realizations ofA.
12:458:30266:17:16:86:539:271:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The underlying source of strategic uncertainty is aptly captured by Proposition 1 for the real economy.
12:459:30369:16:17:72:540:255:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:It is a building block for the analysis of a monetary economy.  The subsequent developments allow debt to
12:460:30474:17:40:72:240:238:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:be held both internally and externally.
12:461:30513:40:27:72:372:198:14:g_d0_f11:14:g_d0_f11:4    Debt Fragility in a Monetary Economy
12:462:30554:27:16:72:540:171:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This section studies the interaction of monetary interventions and debt fragility.  Intuitively, monetary policy
12:463:30666:16:17:72:540:155:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:acts via three channels.  First, it can collect seignorage taxes and supplement the resources collected through
12:464:30777:17:15:72:501:138:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:labor taxation.  Second, by adjusting the realized inflation rate, it can lower the real value of debt.
12:465:30880:15:0:79:375:123:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:16This source of multiplicity is at the heart of Calvo (1988) and Cooper (2012).
13:466:30962:0:17:86:539:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:But, third, there are potential resource costs of funding the government through the inflation tax:  young
13:467:31068:17:17:72:540:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:agents perceiving high inflation in the future will work less,  reducing the monetary tax base.  This effect
13:468:31176:17:17:72:540:725:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:though depends on the extent of discretion in the conduct of monetary policy.  Also, the mean inflation rate
13:469:31284:17:16:72:513:708:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9: ̃πeis priced into the nominal interest rate, which makes attempt to deliver surprise inflation difficult.
13:470:31390:16:17:86:539:692:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Accordingly, this section of the paper is constructed around two polar cases, distinguished by the ability
13:471:31496:17:24:72:236:675:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of the monetary authority to commit.
13:472:31532:24:17:86:540:651:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:i.Monetary delegation: monetary policy decisions are made by an independent central bank that pursues
13:473:31633:17:17:96:539:634:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:a known and explicit rule, independent of fiscal considerations.  We consider the case of strict inflation
13:474:31739:17:24:96:425:617:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:targeting:  the central bank is committed to an unconditional inflation rate.
13:475:31816:24:17:83:539:593:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:ii.Monetary discretion:  monetary and fiscal decisions are linked.  Given the state of the economy, money
13:476:31921:17:17:96:539:576:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:creation and taxes are set so as to minimize welfare costs and tax distortions of old agents given a
13:477:32021:17:24:96:355:559:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:budget constraint.  Default is also chosen optimallyex post.
13:478:32081:24:17:71:539:535:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Before analyzing debt fragility under these monetary regimes, we formally define the equilibrium concept of
13:479:32188:17:33:71:166:518:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the nominal economy.
13:480:32208:33:23:71:354:485:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:4.1    State Variables and Equilibrium Definition
13:481:32257:23:17:71:539:462:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The strategic uncertainty identified in Proposition 1 is modeled through a sunspot variable, denoteds, that
13:482:32364:17:17:72:540:445:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:corresponds to confidence of domestic and foreign households about the repayment of government debt next
13:483:32468:17:24:72:102:428:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:period.
13:484:32475:24:17:88:540:404:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:-  Ifs=so, agents are “optimists” :  they coordinate on the risk free (fundamental) price of the govern-
13:485:32579:17:24:96:143:387:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:ment debt.
13:486:32589:24:17:88:539:363:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:-  Ifs=sp, agents are “pessimists” :  they coordinate on higher risk / lower price equilibria with state
13:487:32693:17:24:96:178:346:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:contingent default.
13:488:32712:24:17:72:540:322:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The distribution of sunspot shocks is i.i.d.  Denote byp∈(0,1) the probability ofs=so.  In the event there
13:489:32818:17:17:72:540:305:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:is a unique equilibrium price, then the fundamental price obtains regardless of the sunspot realization.  Note
13:490:32928:17:16:72:296:288:10:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f12:that we only consider cases where debt has value.17
13:491:32979:16:17:86:540:272:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The state of the economy isS= (A,i,m−1,s,s−1).  Aggregate productivity,A, is realized and directly
13:492:33077:17:17:72:540:255:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:affects the productivity of the old.  There are two endogenous predetermined state variables,m−1andi,
13:493:33178:17:16:72:540:238:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:respectively real money holdings of current old agents, and the nominal interest rate on outstanding public
13:494:33285:16:17:72:539:222:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:debt.   Both  the  sunspot  shock  last  period,s−1,  and  the  current  realization,s,  may  impact  fiscal  policy,
13:495:33402:17:17:72:291:205:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:monetary policy and the choices of private agents.
13:496:33452:17:17:86:539:188:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:To define a Stationary Rational Expectations Equilibrium (SREE), it is necessary to be precise about
13:497:33552:17:16:72:540:171:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:market  clearing  conditions,  the  link  between  money  printing,  inflation  and  seignorage  revenue  and  from
13:498:33667:16:17:72:540:155:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:these,  the  government  budget  constraint.   These  conditions  are  used  in  the  equilibrium  definition  and  in
13:499:33785:17:15:72:244:138:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:constructing various types of equilibria.
13:500:33826:15:0:79:452:123:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:17The case of “market shutdown”, where debt has no value, is not of direct interest for our analysis.
14:501:33929:0:24:72:190:759:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:4.1.1    Market Clearing

14:510:34380:16:17:72:540:626:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:plus the demand from the foreigners is not less than the real stock of government debt.  We assume that the
14:511:34487:17:31:72:464:609:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:foreigners’ endowment is large enough to clear the market for bonds as long as (9) is met.

15:575:36732:24:17:86:539:570:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The welfare criterion of the government will depend on the monetary policy framework, as detailed below.
15:576:36836:17:17:71:539:553:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The polar cases of delegation and discretion are studied within this framework;  the conduct of monetary
15:577:36940:17:17:71:540:536:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:policy determines what the government takes as given in choosing its policy.18Also, we characterize equilibria
15:578:37050:17:16:71:540:519:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:for givenθ, share of government debt held by domestic agents, as its value is not pinned down in equilibrium.
15:579:37159:16:17:86:539:503:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:By making the sunspot binary (optimism or pessimism), we restrict attention to equilibria with potentially
15:580:37265:17:17:71:539:486:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:at most two levels of the nominal interest rate.  As discussed in Section 3, there could be more self-fulfilling
15:581:37377:17:17:71:539:469:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:levels of interest rates associated with different default thresholds.  Allowing the sunspot variable to have
15:582:37486:17:16:71:539:452:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:more  than  two  realizations  could  capture  these  outcomes,  without  changing  the  essential  nature  of  the
15:583:37601:16:34:71:150:436:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:following analysis.
15:584:37620:34:23:71:226:402:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:4.2    Monetary Delegation
15:585:37646:23:17:71:539:379:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:In this institutional structure, the treasury has discretionary power over fiscal policy, choosing fiscal policy
15:586:37758:17:16:71:539:362:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f9:ex postgiven the monetary intervention.  In contrast, the monetary authority is endowed with a commitment
15:587:37863:16:17:71:539:346:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:technology.  We find that under monetary delegation to a strict inflation target, debt fragility remains.  The
15:588:37973:17:17:71:539:329:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:key intuition behind this result is that strict inflation targeting turns a nominal debt contract into a real
15:589:38082:17:17:71:539:312:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:security.  Hence the presence of debt fragility in real economy identified in section 3 persists in the nominal
15:590:38193:17:16:71:242:295:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:economy with strict inflation targeting.
15:591:38233:16:17:86:539:279:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:One interpretation of this structure is that the government of an individual country delegates its monetary
15:592:38340:17:17:71:539:262:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:policy  to  an  independent  central  bank,  by  joining  a  monetary  union  for  instance.   The  central  bank  of
15:593:38457:17:17:71:539:245:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the  union  pursues  an  independent  policy  of  strict  inflation  targeting  and  the  fiscal  authority  is  left  with
15:594:38580:17:16:71:290:228:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:discretionary tax policy choices (taxes or default).
15:595:38632:16:17:86:539:212:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Specifically,  the  central  bank  commits  to  an  inflation  target  0< ̃π∗≤1  and  delivers  it  by  printing
15:596:38744:17:15:71:539:195:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:money.  By doing so, the central bank does not accommodate productivity shocks.  Revenue from seignorage
15:597:38848:15:12:79:540:180:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:18Aguiar, Amador, Farhi, and Gopinath (2013) and Corsetti and Dedola (2013) study discretionary monetary authorities.
15:598:38965:12:10:72:540:168:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:Our analysis will also highlight particular forms of commitment by the central bank as well as the reputation effect necessary
15:599:39091:10:0:72:253:158:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:to implement this solution without commitment.

22:962:55946:24:17:86:539:463:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Proposition 3 is essentially a comparative statics result and thus holds for only a subset of equilibria of
22:963:56053:17:17:72:540:446:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the debt financing problem, i.e.  those that are locally stable under best response dynamics.  A locally stable
22:964:56164:17:17:72:540:429:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:equilibrium  is  indicated  in  Figure  1  and  refers  to  the  determination  of  the  interest  rate  on  debt  and  the
22:965:56287:17:16:72:528:412:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:default cut-off.  The relative slopes of the two curves at this point are used in the proof of Proposition 3.
22:966:56396:16:17:86:539:396:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This section studies debt fragility when the monetary authority commits to a strict inflation target.  As
22:967:56501:17:17:72:540:379:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the environment does not feature any ex post cost of inflation, the central bank could be tempted to deviate,
22:968:56610:17:17:72:540:362:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:inflate  beyond  expectations  and  thus  steal  the  benefits  of  predetermined  real  money  balances.   Still,  this
22:969:56730:17:16:72:540:345:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:policy could be sustained with a reputational mechanism that takes full demonetization of the economy as
22:970:56834:16:17:72:540:329:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the punishment for deviating from the inflation target.  Indeed, the welfare in the real economy is lower than
22:971:56944:17:17:72:540:312:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the welfare in the monetary economy.  We formally discuss this class of reputational mechanisms in Section
22:972:57050:17:33:72:87:295:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:5.2.
22:973:57054:33:24:72:225:262:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:4.3    Monetary Discretion
22:974:57080:24:16:72:540:238:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Does  monetary  discretion  insulate  against  debt  fragility?   Intuitively,  a  discretionary  policy  maker  could
22:975:57198:16:17:72:540:222:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:adjust inflation and seignorage to accommodate variations in the price of government debt driven by strategic
22:976:57307:17:17:72:203:205:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:uncertainty and avoid default.
22:977:57337:17:16:86:539:188:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:In a monetary discretion regime, the government has full discretionary power over both monetary and
22:978:57436:16:17:72:540:172:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:fiscal policy.  It designs its policy (τ(S), ̃π(S),D(S)) in every state, as a best response to realized productivity
22:979:57552:17:17:71:539:155:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:shockA,  the sunspots (s−1,s) and predetermined variables of the economym−1andi.  The government
22:980:57648:17:0:71:539:138:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:maximizes the welfare of home agents.  This is, in effect, the same as minimizing the cost of its policy to
23:981:57757:0:17:72:540:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:taxpayers, hence to old agents, since they contribute to government’s resources via the tax on labor income
23:982:57864:17:17:72:220:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:and seignorage on money holding.
23:983:57896:17:17:86:540:725:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:In an environment with discretion, money creation provides anex postsource of revenue without creating
23:984:57998:17:16:72:540:708:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:any distortion.  This low social cost of revenue ought to reduce the likelihood of default and stabilize debt
23:985:58107:16:17:72:101:692:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:values.
23:986:58114:17:17:86:539:675:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:But, an essential element of this environment is the interaction between expected and realized inflation.
23:987:58219:17:17:72:540:658:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Specifically, if agents anticipate high inflation (low  ̃πe), they would reduce labor supply in youth and their
23:988:58330:17:16:72:539:641:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:real  money  holdingsm−1accordingly.   To  collect  revenue  from  seignorage,  the  central  bank  then  has  to
23:989:58443:16:17:72:540:625:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:deliver a higher inflation rate (low  ̃π), consistent with the initial beliefs of agents.  Hence, under discretion,
23:990:58558:17:17:72:540:608:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the capacity of the central bank to support a stressed fiscal authority may be compromised by the strategic
23:991:58665:17:17:72:540:591:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:complementarity between expected inflation and delivered inflation:  if agents anticipate the willingness of
23:992:58773:17:16:72:540:574:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the central bank to resort to inflation, the real money tax base would decrease, which in turn reduces the
23:993:58879:16:17:72:252:558:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:capacity of the central bank to intervene.
23:994:58921:17:17:86:540:541:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The formation of expectations by young agents reflects theseex  postpolicy choices.  Let   ̃πe(S) denote
23:995:59025:17:16:72:540:524:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the  expectation  of  future  (inverse)  inflation  given  the  current  stateS.   Then  the  requirement  of  rational
23:996:59144:16:17:71:540:508:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:expectations is  ̃πe(S) =ES′|S ̃π(S′) where the expectation is over the future state givenS.  This condition
23:997:59252:17:17:72:342:491:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:will be used in the construction of equilibria under discretion.
23:998:59316:17:17:86:539:474:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:To characterize a SREE under discretion, we first determine the policy choices of a discretionary policy
23:999:59420:17:16:72:540:457:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:maker, then analyze the debt pricing dimension of the equilibrium and the associated stationary inflation
23:1000:59525:16:31:72:332:441:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:expectations.  The SREE combines these essential elements.
23:1001:59583:31:23:72:347:410:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:4.3.1    Choice Problem of a Discretionary Government

24:1036:61434:16:17:72:461:519:10:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f12:lie in the strategic interaction between expected and realized inflation under discretion.28
24:1037:61526:17:17:86:539:502:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:If the government chooses to repay the debt, the real money tax basem−1is given.  Its policy is naturally

24:1041:61957:17:17:72:540:435:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:cover its obligations, the government must impose a labor tax if it chooses to avoid default.  Under discretion,
24:1042:62069:17:16:72:540:418:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the government relies primarily on seignorage revenue to service debt.  This characterization is summarized
24:1043:62176:16:17:72:127:402:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:in Lemma 3.

24:1045:62298:17:17:72:540:368:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:function:  when  default  occurs,  monetary  policy  is  implemented  via  lump-sum  transfers  which  are  purely
24:1046:62412:17:16:72:540:351:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:redistributive, and consequently has no influence on the choices of the government.  We set   ̃πd=  ̃πin the

26:1142:67562:17:17:86:539:488:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Suppose investors believe the government will default on its debt with positive probability.  If the belief is
26:1143:67672:17:17:71:540:471:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:self-fulfilling, then the optimal policy of the government must be to set the inflation level to  ̃πfor allAwhether

26:1145:67895:16:17:72:539:438:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:and interest on debt for all realization ofA, and default would be avoided.  Hence, inflation expectations of
26:1146:68004:17:17:72:539:421:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:agents are consistent with the best response of the government at   ̃πe(sp) =  ̃π.  The no-arbitrage condition
26:1147:68114:17:30:72:197:404:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:pricing public debt becomes:

26:1157:68349:17:16:72:540:309:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:librium  condition,  one  of  which  carries  a  risk-premium  and  induces  the  government  to  default  for  some

26:1161:68752:17:16:72:540:234:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of the best response of the discretionary government.  In particular, the interest rate with a risk-premium
26:1162:68859:16:17:72:540:218:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:that  solves  the  no-arbitrage  condition  is  systematically  associated  with  the  lowest  real  money  tax  base
26:1163:68976:17:15:72:506:201:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f9:m=  ̃πe(sp) =  ̃π, which in turn prevents the central bank from inflating away the real value of debt.
26:1164:69078:15:13:79:540:186:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:29In general   ̃πe(S) denotes expected (inverse) inflation.  The notation   ̃πe(s) highlights the dependence of expectations on
26:1165:69205:13:9:72:540:173:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:the sunspot,s.  This is the expectation held by young agents regarding the future value of  ̃π.  This value determines the labor
26:1166:69333:9:0:72:464:164:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:supply and real money demand of young poor agents.  It also influences the nominal interest rate, see (9).
27:1167:69441:0:24:72:218:759:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:4.3.3    Inflation Expectations
27:1168:69472:24:16:72:540:735:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:We now turn to the third component of the equilibrium:  the determinants of inflation expectations   ̃πe(s).
27:1169:69580:16:17:72:540:719:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This  section  establishes  two  results.   First,  there  exist  inflation  expectations,  contingent  on  the  sunspot
27:1170:69700:17:17:72:540:702:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:realization,  that  are  consistent  with  the  choices  of  the  government.   Second,  there  may  be  multiple  such
27:1171:69819:17:17:72:540:685:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:levels  of  inflationary  expectations.   This  last  point  arises  from  the  complementarities  between  monetary
27:1172:69935:17:16:72:218:668:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:expectations and policy response.
27:1173:69968:16:17:86:539:652:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:As shown in the proof of Lemma 4, in the event of pessimism, young agents expect high inflation, i.e.
27:1174:70069:17:17:72:540:635:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9: ̃πe(sp)  =   ̃π.   That  is,  whenever  the  equilibrium  of  the  debt  financing  problem  induces  state-contingent
27:1175:70188:17:17:72:539:618:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:default, the inflation rate is maximal.  So, regardless of the current stateS, given pessimism in the previous
27:1176:70298:17:16:71:539:601:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:period,s−1=sp, the inverse inflation rate is  ̃π(S) =  ̃π.  This is then consistent with the initial expectations
27:1177:70411:16:17:71:457:585:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of the current old, formed when they were young in the previous period, i.e.   ̃πe(sp) =  ̃π.
27:1178:70504:17:17:86:539:568:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The  issues  of  existence  and  multiplicity  of  inflation  expectations  arise  whens−1=so.   From  Lemma
27:1179:70612:17:16:72:540:551:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:4,  young agents anticipate the government will service its debt obligation for allS.  The question is then
27:1180:70719:16:17:71:539:535:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:how the government will repay its obligation.  Given the bias toward inflationary financing of debt,  what
27:1181:70825:17:17:71:539:518:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:determines  ̃πe(so) is whether seignorage resource is enough to service principal and interest on debt for all
27:1182:70935:17:17:71:540:501:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:(A,s).  If the debt is not too large, then the inflation tax alone is sufficient to cover debt obligations:  i.e.
27:1183:71048:17:16:72:540:484:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9: ̃πr(A,s,·)> ̃πfor all (A,s) and   ̃πe(so)> ̃π.  In this case,τ(A,s) = 0 for all (A,s).  Else, the inflation tax
27:1184:71160:16:17:72:528:468:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:will be maximal,  ̃πe(so) =  ̃π, and supplemented by a labor tax.  In both casesD(A,s,) =rfor all (A,s).

29:1249:75107:0:24:72:251:759:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f8:4.3.4    Equilibrium characterization
29:1250:75144:24:16:72:540:735:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The analysis has established the government budget constraint under discretion, the potential for multiple
29:1251:75250:16:17:72:540:719:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:solutions to the debt valuation equation and the existence of inflation expectations consistent with monetary
29:1252:75359:17:17:72:540:702:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:policy.  Taken together, these elements create the basis for sunspot equilibria associated with the valuation
29:1253:75468:17:25:72:204:685:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of government debt.  Formally,
29:1254:75498:25:16:72:539:660:10:g_d0_f8:10:g_d0_f10:Proposition 4.For  any ̃π>0,  under  Assumptions  2  and  3,  there  is  a  SREE  under  discretion  with  the
29:1255:75608:16:25:72:160:644:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:following properties:
29:1256:75629:25:25:83:524:619:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:1.  Ifs−1=so, government debt is risk free as the treasury reimburses with probability 1, with either:
29:1257:75731:25:20:105:519:594:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:a.  if0< b <ˆb, then ̃πe(so)> ̃πand for allAalls, ̃π(A,s,·)> ̃π,τ(A,s,·) = 0,D(A,s,·) =r,
29:1258:75820:20:25:106:519:574:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:b.  ifˆb≤b < ̄b, then ̃πe(so) =  ̃πand for allAalls, ̃π(A,s,·) =  ̃π,τ(A,s,·)>0,D(A,s,·) =r.
29:1259:75912:25:17:83:540:549:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:2.  Ifs−1=sp, the interest rate incorporates a risk-premium.  For allA, ̃π(A,·) =  ̃π.  The treasury defaults
29:1260:76021:17:25:96:363:532:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f10:on its debt for allA < ̄Awhere ̄A∈(Al,Ah)and ̃πe(sp) =  ̃π.
29:1261:76080:25:16:72:540:507:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f9:Proof.We describe the optimal behavior of agents consistent with the equilibrium definition.  This proof
29:1262:76184:16:17:72:540:491:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:builds on Lemma 4 and the existence of several interest rates (and associated inflation expectations) consis-
29:1263:76293:17:17:72:229:474:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:tent with the equilibrium definition.
29:1264:76330:17:16:86:540:457:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Ifs−1=so, then by Assumption 3, debt is risk free.  Two cases need to be distinguished, as established
29:1265:76432:16:17:72:539:441:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:in  Lemma  5.   Ifb <ˆb,  then  inflation  expectations  under  optimism   ̃πe(so)  allow  seignorage  resource  to
29:1266:76547:17:17:71:539:424:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:be sufficient to service principal and interest on debt.  Young agents form expectations of no default and
29:1267:76653:17:17:72:540:407:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9: ̃πe(so)> ̃π.  They supply labor accordingly,  young agents with low productivity save with money,  young
29:1268:76758:17:16:72:539:390:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:rich agents save via intermediated claims;  the interest rateion the government security satisfies the no-
29:1269:76864:16:17:72:539:374:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:arbitrage condition (9) with a zero probability of default, i.e.Pd= 0, and  ̃πe(so).  The optimal policy of the
29:1270:76975:17:17:71:460:357:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:government is then to set for allA, alls,  ̃π(A,s,·)> ̃π,τ(A,s,·) = 0 and repay the debt.
29:1271:77064:17:17:86:539:340:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:On the other hand,  ifˆb≤b < ̄b, then there is an equilibrium with   ̃πe(so) =   ̃π, seignorage resource is
29:1272:77171:17:16:72:540:323:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:not sufficient and taxes need be raised to service debt.  Using Lemma 3 and Assumption 3, for allA, alls,
29:1273:77276:16:17:72:539:307:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9: ̃π(A,s,·) =  ̃π,τ(A,s,·) solves the government budget constraint (51) and debt is repaid.  Accordingly, young
29:1274:77386:17:17:72:540:290:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:agents form expectationsPd= 0,   ̃πe(so) =  ̃π, the government security is priced according to (9).  In both
29:1275:77494:17:17:72:175:273:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:cases, all markets clear.
29:1276:77519:17:16:86:540:256:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Fors−1=sp,  we  detail  only  the  differences  with  the  previous  case.   Independently  of  the  level  ofb,
29:1277:77631:16:17:72:539:240:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:young agents form rational expectations in which there is a positive probability of default, i.e.Pd>0, and
29:1278:77737:17:17:72:540:223:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9: ̃πe(sp) =   ̃π.  The government security is priced accordingly.  Giveniand seignorage revenueνm ̃π(1− ̃π),
29:1279:77844:17:17:71:540:206:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:there is a unique threshold ̄A(i)> Alsuch that the optimal policy is to raise labor taxesτfor allA≥ ̄A(i)
29:1280:77949:17:16:71:539:189:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:so as to satisfy the budget constraint (51) and default otherwise.  Finally, expectations are consistent with
29:1281:78058:16:25:71:300:173:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the best response of the government:Pd=F( ̄A(i)).
29:1282:78107:25:17:86:539:148:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Does monetary discretion provide a shield against debt fragility?  Can the government inflate the real
29:1283:78209:17:0:72:540:131:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:value of debt and generate additional resources to service its debt? The answer is negative. As the proposition
30:1284:78322:0:17:72:540:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:makes clear, this result does not hinge upon a particular inflation ceiling  ̃π.32Indeed, when pessimism hits
30:1285:78431:17:17:72:540:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the economy, the interplay between inflation expectations and real money tax basecornersthe central bank
30:1286:78535:17:17:72:540:725:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:into  a  high  inflation  regime  with  no  more  capacity  to  inflate  debt  or  provide  additional  resources  to  the
30:1287:78657:17:16:72:540:708:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:treasury.  Hence, under monetary discretion, the sunspot shock to investors confidence triggers a joint shift
30:1288:78766:16:17:72:540:692:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:in inflation expectations and debt sustainability.  This shift in inflation expectations is the driving force that
30:1289:78880:17:17:72:540:675:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:neutralizes the strategy of the discretionary government to print money and collect seignorage to service its
30:1290:78989:17:17:72:94:658:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:debt.
30:1291:78994:17:16:86:539:641:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Finally, the strategic complementarity between expected and delivered inflation may give rise to inflation
30:1292:79100:16:17:72:540:625:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:multiplicity, as discussed in sub-section 4.3.3.  This element is not explicit in Proposition 4.  The point of the
30:1293:79214:17:17:72:540:608:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:proposition, and of this paper, is to study the interaction of debt fragility and monetary policy.  Accordingly,
30:1294:79326:17:17:72:540:591:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the analysis in Proposition 4 rests on the selection of a particular equilibrium in the event of optimism, i.e.
30:1295:79437:17:16:72:540:574:10:g_d0_f16:10:g_d0_f9:s−1=so.  The equilibrium selection is orthogonal to the multiple solutions of the debt pricing equation, as
30:1296:79544:16:17:72:540:558:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:argued before.  Of course, it is possible to add another, independent, dimension to the problem by introducing
30:1297:79654:17:40:72:353:541:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:strategic uncertainty over the the inflation rate, given optimism.
30:1298:79720:40:27:72:295:501:14:g_d0_f11:14:g_d0_f11:5Leaning Against the Winds
30:1299:79746:27:16:72:540:474:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:These  results  make  clear  that  the  monetary  authority  may  be  unable  to  prevent  debt  fragility.   If  there
30:1300:79865:16:17:72:540:458:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:is a commitment to an unconditional inflation target,  the environment is similar to a real economy,  thus
30:1301:79971:17:17:72:540:441:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:exposing the debt to multiple valuations.  If the monetary authority has complete discretion, then it will use
30:1302:80081:17:17:72:539:424:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the inflation tax to raise revenueex postand again fiscal tools may be needed to finance debt repayments.  In
30:1303:80190:17:16:72:540:407:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:both cases, when productivity is low, the tax burden can become excessive leading to default.  In equilibrium,
30:1304:80300:16:17:72:442:391:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:the valuation of debt will be subject to investor sentiments in a sunspot equilibrium.
30:1305:80386:17:17:86:539:374:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This section considers a more nuanced monetary intervention which is accommodative during periods of
30:1306:80486:17:17:72:540:357:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:low productivity.  We show that with commitment, this intervention eliminates debt fragility.  Further, we
30:1307:80592:17:16:72:540:340:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:provide conditions such that reputation effects are strong enough to support this outcome without commit-
30:1308:80697:16:34:72:97:324:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:ment.
30:1309:80702:34:23:72:309:290:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:5.1    Stabilization through Commitment
30:1310:80741:23:17:72:540:267:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This section returns to the commitment case.  Instead of imposing an inflation target, we allow the central
30:1311:80848:17:16:72:540:250:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:bank to choose a state-contingent inflation policy that alters the real debt burden and distributes resources
30:1312:80957:16:17:72:540:234:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:from seignorage across states.  As in Chari, Christiano, and Eichenbaum (1998) this is a one period com-
30:1313:81061:17:17:72:540:217:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:mitment,  allowing  the  monetary  authority  to  commit  to  inflation  next  period,  contingent  on  the  current
30:1314:81177:17:17:72:540:200:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:state.   By  carefully  choosing  the  distribution  of  realized  future  inflation,  the  central  bank  can  provide  a
30:1315:81299:17:16:72:193:183:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:shield against debt fragility.
30:1316:81329:16:17:86:539:167:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Suppose  the  monetary  authority  commits  to  a  rule  given  by   ̃π(A,i,s−1):  the  rate  of  inflation  in  the
30:1317:81445:17:15:72:540:150:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:current period depends on current productivity, the interest rate on outstanding debt as well as the sunspot
30:1318:81553:15:0:79:410:135:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:32Specifically, it holds for  ̃πarbitrarily close to 0, i.e.  an inflation ceiling arbitrarily high.
31:1319:81655:0:17:72:539:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:realization from previous period.33This rule is devised with a couple of key properties.  First,  to induce
31:1320:81762:17:17:72:540:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:agents to hold money, the rule will deliver a target rate of inflation.  Second, it will support the fundamental
31:1321:81874:17:17:72:540:725:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:equilibrium  by  using  monetary  tools  to  counter  pessimistic  expectations  so  that  equilibria  with  strategic
31:1322:81992:17:16:72:539:708:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:uncertainty no longer exist.34In this way, the monetary authority responds to variations in current beliefs,
31:1323:82100:16:17:72:540:692:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:reflected in the sunspot and the interest rate, by appropriately setting policy for the future.  Importantly, if
31:1324:82212:17:17:72:540:675:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:investors were pessimistic in the previous period, this policy responds to variations in productivity:  the rate
31:1325:82324:17:17:72:540:658:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:of inflation is inversely related to current productivity.  Specifically, whenAis high, the rate of inflation is
31:1326:82436:17:16:72:540:641:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:relatively low and fiscal policy, through the setting of tax rates, bears more of the burden of financing debt
31:1327:82546:16:17:72:540:625:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:obligations.  But during times of low productivity, when default is likely, the monetary authority inflates the
31:1328:82657:17:17:72:540:608:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:real value of debt and generates seignorage revenue.  Both effects allow the fiscal authority to set low taxes
31:1329:82767:17:17:72:151:591:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:and avoid default.
31:1330:82785:17:16:86:539:574:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:We first describe the desired properties of this policy, derive its existence and properties in Lemma 6.
31:1331:82889:16:17:72:540:558:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Then,  we  characterize  the  stationary  equilibrium  of  the  economy  under   ̃π(A,i,s−1)  and  argue  that  such
31:1332:83005:17:17:72:286:541:10:g_d0_f9:7:g_d0_f12:monetary policy rule stabilizes debt valuations.35
31:1333:83055:17:16:86:539:524:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Specifically, suppose the central bank commits to a rule in which   ̃π(A,i,so) =   ̃π∗for all (A,i):  under
31:1334:83162:16:17:71:540:508:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:optimism, there is an inflation target as inmonetary delegation.  Delivered inflation  ̃π∗is independent of both
31:1335:83274:17:17:71:540:491:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:current productivityAand the interest rate on debt.  Whens−1=sp, the central bank implements a state
31:1336:83374:17:17:71:539:474:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:dependent (on (A,i)) monetary policy, labelled‘law’, forleaning against the winds.  This policy satisfies two

34:1470:90945:62:17:86:539:456:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:This proposition makes clear that the commitment of the central bank rules out the effect of pessimism

34:1474:91349:17:17:72:540:389:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:Proposition 5.38In the cases−1=sp, note the distribution of inflation over realization ofA:  for lowA,
34:1475:91451:17:17:71:539:372:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:high  inflation,  i.e.   low  real  value  of  debt  and  high  seignorage  revenue.   Hence,  in  case  of  pessimism,  the
34:1476:91575:17:16:71:539:355:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:monetary authority implements a countercyclical policy that stabilizes the price of debt and provides fiscal
34:1477:91683:16:17:71:539:339:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:relief for low values ofA, compensated by lower inflation for higher realizations ofA.  A critical element of
34:1478:91792:17:17:71:539:322:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:this policy is the commitment of the central bank so that inflation expectations are anchored and the real
34:1479:91898:17:17:71:539:305:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:money tax base is not sensitive to variations in private agents sentiments.  It illustrates how the central bank
34:1480:92010:17:16:71:539:288:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:can  alter  the  real  value  of  debt,  and  incidentally  distribute  income  from  seignorage,  so  as  to  contain  the
34:1481:92133:16:17:71:540:272:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f10:fiscal pressure that weights on the fiscal authority.  In this sense, the monetary authorityleans  against  the
34:1482:92244:17:17:71:373:255:10:g_d0_f10:10:g_d0_f9:windsof pessimism as well as those associated with low productivity.
34:1483:92312:17:17:86:539:238:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:As written, the monetary intervention depends jointly on the sunspot from the previous period as well
34:1484:92413:17:16:71:539:221:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:as the interest on outstanding debt.  Along the equilibrium path, from Proposition 5, only the fundamental
34:1485:92519:16:17:71:539:205:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:price of debt will be observed.  Though extraneous uncertainty may still exist, it will not be reflected in the
34:1486:92630:17:17:71:539:188:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:equilibrium interest rates.  With this in mind, it may be more natural to condition monetary interventions
34:1487:92736:17:17:71:539:171:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:on interest rates so that along the equilibrium path, no actual intervention is needed.  But, the monetary
34:1488:92842:17:14:71:539:154:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:authority stands ready to intervene in response to higher interest rates that reflect investor pessimism.  This
34:1489:92953:14:0:79:444:140:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:38The dependence oniis not explicit as these are the policy functions along the equilibrium path.
35:1490:93052:0:17:72:540:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:is, in effect, a threat of the monetary authority off the equilibrium path to intervene either to support the
35:1491:93161:17:17:72:447:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:fiscal authority or, if interest rates are too high, to allow default with probability one.

35:1516:94299:33:24:72:308:415:12:g_d0_f11:12:g_d0_f11:5.2    Stabilization without Commitment
35:1517:94338:24:16:72:540:391:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The preceding analysis assumes that the monetary authority is granted the capacity to commit to policies
35:1518:94442:16:17:72:540:375:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:and argues that this power can eliminate multiplicity.  This section replaces the assumption of commitment
35:1519:94548:17:17:72:539:358:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:with  an  equilibrium  response  to  deviations  from’wit’that  can,  in  principle,  support  this  policy  without
35:1520:94664:17:16:71:539:341:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:commitment.  The argument uses a version of the grim trigger strategy in repeated games, as in Rubinstein
35:1521:94769:16:17:71:539:325:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:(1979).  We focus on certain features of the economy, such as the presence of strategic uncertainty, that make
35:1522:94879:17:17:71:540:308:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:deviations from policy’wit’costly and thus support the elimination of debt fragility as an outcome without
35:1523:94985:17:17:71:128:291:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:commitment.
35:1524:94996:17:16:86:539:274:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The monetary authority has an incentive to deviate from its committed policy to take advantage of the
35:1525:95097:16:17:71:539:258:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:non-distortionary nature of the inflation tax.  To counter this gain,  we construct an equilibrium in which
35:1526:95204:17:17:71:540:241:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:any deviations from’wit’are met by a strict application of ’dlg’, the monetary delegation regime of strict
35:1527:95310:17:17:71:539:224:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:inflation targeting.  From Section 4.2, this generates lifetime welfare for each generation ofVdlg( ̃π∗,p), given
35:1528:95423:17:16:71:388:207:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:by (43), and which depends positively onp, the probability of optimism.
35:1529:95494:16:17:86:539:191:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:The construction, formalized in Proposition 6, goes as follows.  Along the equilibrium path the monetary
35:1530:95598:17:17:71:539:174:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:authority follows’wit’described in (68).  This generates lifetime welfare ofVwit( ̃π∗).  In a given state, the
35:1531:95708:17:15:71:539:157:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:central  bank  can  deviate  and  consider  any  policy  whatsoever:  this  is  modeled  as  complete  discretion  for
35:1532:95826:15:12:79:540:142:6:g_d0_f15:8:g_d0_f14:39In other words, committing to a strategy allows the monetary authority a second mover-advantage while anchoring expec-
35:1533:95946:12:0:72:182:130:8:g_d0_f14:8:g_d0_f14:tations in this dynamic game.
36:1534:95977:0:17:72:539:759:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:a single period, which is the most profitable deviation.  After that deviation, the’whatever  it  takes’type
36:1535:96085:17:17:72:540:742:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f9:intervention is no longer credible.  The monetary authority returns to its essential mandate of a targeted
36:1536:96191:17:17:72:236:725:10:g_d0_f9:10:g_d0_f10:inflation rate  ̃π∗, labelled’delegation’.
